    } else {

            "userconsent": $userConsent,
            "specialization": "Pediatrics",
        })
    }
    catch(err){
        console.log(err)
    }

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/templates/jsp/pb2/js/plugin/thiss-ds.js" nonce="6ddbb0cf98f64ddeb8a247f5ddbeb272"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="6ddbb0cf98f64ddeb8a247f5ddbeb272">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '5a9cfb0b-f0b8-4c59-adca-2907da031698'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" id="abstract-graphical-en">
         <h2 id="d54212446" class="article-section__header section__title graphical abstractlang_en graphical">Graphical Abstract</h2>
         <div class="graphical-abstract">
            <p><b>One material fits both</b>: An aqueous symmetric sodium-ion battery is constructed with the NASICON-structured Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> with the redox couples of Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> and Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>2+</sup> working on the anode and cathode sides, respectively. The symmetric Na-ion battery exhibits well-defined voltage plateaus located within the electrochemical window of an aqueous electrolyte with stable cycling performance and superior rate capability.
            </p><figure>
               <div class="center graphic__image"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/b1e06102-0047-48e0-a541-5cc3ae5ae447/anie201606508-toc-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/b1e06102-0047-48e0-a541-5cc3ae5ae447/anie201606508-toc-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/4106aefe-d3bd-4d36-8a9e-d310ae1b94dc/anie201606508-toc-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/b1e06102-0047-48e0-a541-5cc3ae5ae447/anie201606508-toc-0001-m.jpg" alt="Description unavailable" title="Description unavailable" loading="lazy"></picture></a><p class="caption-style"></p>
               </div>
            </figure>
            <p></p>
            </div>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d54212473" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>A symmetric sodium-ion battery with an aqueous electrolyte is demonstrated; it utilizes the NASICON-structured Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as both the anode and the cathode. The NASICON-structured Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> possesses two electrochemically active transition metals with the redox couples of Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> and Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>2+</sup> working on the anode and cathode sides, respectively. The symmetric cell based on this bipolar electrode material exhibits a well-defined voltage plateau centered at about 1.4 V in an aqueous electrolyte with a stable cycle performance and superior rate capability. The advent of aqueous symmetric sodium-ion battery with high safety and low cost may provide a solution for large-scale stationary energy storage.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="anie201606508-sec-0001">
         
         <p>The development of electric-power storage devices, with the characteristics of low cost, high-energy-density, and long cycle life, is a global priority to integrate renewable and clean electric-power generated from solar and wind energy into a smart electrical grid.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0001_R_d54212395e320" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Nature">1</a>-<a href="#anie201606508-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0003_R_d54212395e320" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - J. Power Sources">3</a></sup></span> Despite the great achievement of lithium-ion batteries in portable electronics and electric vehicles in recent years, the insufficient and unevenly distributed lithium resources as well as increasing cost may restrict their application in large-scale electrical energy storage systems.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0004_R_d54212395e322" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Chem. Rev.">4</a>-<a href="#anie201606508-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0007_R_d54212395e322" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. Angew. Chem.">7</a></sup></span> Consequently, extensive efforts have been devoted to the investigation of sodium-ion batteries with nonaqueous electrolytes that share similar scientific and technological principles to the commercialized lithium-ion batteries.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0008_R_d54212395e324" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Nat. Mater.">8</a>-<a href="#anie201606508-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0013_R_d54212395e324" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">13</a></sup></span> Although the utilization of organic liquid electrolytes enables sodium-ion batteries with a higher voltage and a wider choice of electrode materials, safety and environmental concerns are arising from the toxic and flammable organic solvents.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0014_R_d54212395e326" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Energy Environ. Sci.">14</a>, <a href="#anie201606508-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0015_R_d54212395e326" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. Angew. Chem.">15</a></sup></span> Furthermore, compared with aqueous electrolytes, the much lower ionic conductivities and higher costs of organic liquid electrolytes possibly impose additional constrains on large-scale application of nonaqueous sodium-ion batteries. To overcome the drawbacks of organic liquid electrolytes, the development of sodium-ion batteries with aqueous electrolytes may represent a promising approach for large-scale storage of electrical energy.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0016_R_d54212395e328" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Energy Technol.">16</a>-<a href="#anie201606508-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0019_R_d54212395e328" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - J. Power Sources">19</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>Recently, a number of transition metal oxides, Prussian blue analogues, and polyanionic frameworks have demonstrated stable sodium storage performance in aqueous electrolytes.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0020_R_d54212395e332" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Sci. Adv.">20</a>-<a href="#anie201606508-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0024_R_d54212395e332" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - RSC Adv.">24</a></sup></span> Particular interests have also been focused on sodium storage in NASICON (Na Super Ionic Conductors)-type compounds because of their structural stability, their large ionic channels, and the abundance of sodium-insertion sites.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0025_R_d54212395e334" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - J. Phys. Chem. C">25</a>-<a href="#anie201606508-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0027_R_d54212395e334" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Electrochem. Commun.">27</a></sup></span> The NASICON-structured materials with the formula unit of A<sub><i>x</i></sub>M<sub><i>y</i></sub>(XO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, where A, M and X are alkali metal, transition metal and nonmetal atoms, respectively, can be described as three-dimensional polyanionic frameworks of corner sharing MO<sub>6</sub> octahedra and XO<sub>4</sub> tetrahedra with interconnected channels for the diffusion of alkali ions.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0028_R_d54212395e351" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Mater. Res. Bull.">28</a>, <a href="#anie201606508-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0029_R_d54212395e351" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - J. Power Sources">29</a></sup></span> The redox potentials of NASICON-structured materials can be tuned by changing the elemental composition and/or the valence states of the transition metal ions.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0030_R_d54212395e353" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">30</a></sup></span> The NASICON-structured NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> has a sodium-ion insertion potential well-above the evolution of H<sub>2</sub> in an aqueous Na<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> electrolyte.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0031_R_d54212395e368" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">31</a></sup></span> The recently synthesized Na<sub>3</sub>Ti<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as a sodium-bearing anode for aqueous sodium-ion batteries enables the utilization of sodium-depleted cathode materials.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0032_R_d54212395e379" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Electrochem. Commun.">32</a></sup></span> Sodium-ion full-cells with aqueous electrolytes were also constructed with the NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> anode and a variety of cathodes, including Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>,<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0033_R_d54212395e392" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Adv. Energy Mater.">33</a></sup></span> Na<sub>2</sub>NiFe(CN)<sub>6</sub>,<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0034_R_d54212395e399" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Electrochem. Commun.">34</a></sup></span> Na<sub>2</sub>CuFe(CN)<sub>6</sub>,<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0035_R_d54212395e405" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - ChemSusChem">35</a></sup></span> Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO)<sub>4</sub>,<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0036_R_d54212395e414" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Electrochim. Acta">36</a></sup></span> and NaMnO<sub>2</sub>.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0037_R_d54212395e418" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - J. Mater. Chem. A">37</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>In this work, a NASICON-type compound of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> was prepared to construct an aqueous symmetric sodium-ion battery. The design of a symmetric battery is attractive because the cathode and anode with the same active material can simplify the fabrication process, reduce the manufacturing costs, and buffer the volume change of electrodes (the cathode shrinking accompanied by anode expansion, and vice versa).<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0038_R_d54212395e428" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Electrochim. Acta">38</a>, <a href="#anie201606508-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0039_R_d54212395e428" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">39</a></sup></span> Recently, the layered metal oxides of O3-Na<sub>0.8</sub>Ni<sub>0.4</sub>Ti<sub>0.6</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and P2-Na<sub>0.66</sub>Ni<sub>0.17</sub>Co<sub>0.17</sub>Ti<sub>0.66</sub>O<sub>2</sub> were successfully used to realize symmetric sodium-ion batteries through the utilization of the redox centers of nickel and cobalt on the cathode side and titanium on the anode side in organic liquid electrolytes.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0040_R_d54212395e450" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Energy Environ. Sci.">40</a>, <a href="#anie201606508-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0041_R_d54212395e450" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. Angew. Chem.">41</a></sup></span> The realization of an aqueous symmetric sodium-ion battery requires the discovery of an electrode material that can be used as a sodium-rich cathode and a sodium-deficient anode, with sufficient sodium storage capacities, reversible redox activities, and especially working within the electrochemical potential window of water (within the oxygen and hydrogen evolution potentials). The NASICON-type Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> forms a three-dimensional framework based on MnO<sub>6</sub> or TiO<sub>6</sub> octahedra sharing all of its corners with PO<sub>4</sub> tetrahedra (Figure <a href="#anie201606508-fig-0001">1</a>). Two independent types of sodium ions are located in the interstitial sites of the framework with two different oxygen environments: A single interstitial site per formula unit with six-fold coordination (M1 site) is occupied by a less-mobile sodium-ion, and three equivalent sites per formula unit with eight-fold coordination (M2 sites) are occupied by two mobile sodium-ions. Since the sodium ions positioned at M1 sites are strongly bound to the coordinated oxygen atoms, only the sodium ions residing at M2 sites can be extracted/inserted for electrochemical activity.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0042_R_d54212395e467" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Phys. Chem. Chem. Phys.">42</a></sup></span> We demonstrated that the extraction of one sodium-ion per formula unit from Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> with the formation of Na<sub>2</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> through the Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>2+</sup> redox couple is well-below the oxygen evolution potential, and the insertion of one sodium-ion per formula unit into Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> with the formation of Na<sub>4</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> through the Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> redox couple is well-above the hydrogen evolution potential in the neutral aqueous electrolyte of Na<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> (1.0 <span class="smallCaps">m</span>). Therefore, Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> enables its utilization as both a sodium-rich cathode and a sodium-deficient anode for a symmetric sodium-ion battery in the aqueous electrolyte.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="anie201606508-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/e5b54d9d-36ae-4de6-b513-532e3fce8c23/anie201606508-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/e5b54d9d-36ae-4de6-b513-532e3fce8c23/anie201606508-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/dc8b5f3d-d42b-4573-9bf8-53256df76ae9/anie201606508-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/e5b54d9d-36ae-4de6-b513-532e3fce8c23/anie201606508-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=anie201606508-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.201606508" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>Schematic illustration of the aqueous symmetric sodium-ion battery with the NASICON-structured Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as the anode and the cathode.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> was synthesized by a sol-gel method followed by calcination of the precursor at 600 °C in argon atmosphere. The XRD diffraction pattern (Figure <a href="#anie201606508-fig-0002">2</a>) of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> can be indexed into a rhombohedral NASICON-type unit cell with the <img alt="urn:x-wiley:14337851:media:anie201606508:anie201606508-math-0001" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/93ce4f00-6373-4037-89e3-01540df41144/anie201606508-math-0001.png">
 space group (Table S1, Supporting Information). The morphology of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> was analyzed by scanning electron microscopy (SEM) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM). SEM images showed that the particle size of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> ranges from a few hundreds of nanometers to several micrometers. TEM images revealed that the Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> particles are composed of nanosized primary particles well-dispersed in a carbon matrix. The presence of carbon is used to improve the electrical conductivity of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>. The carbon content is about 7.8 wt.%, determined by thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) of the Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> sample. The chemical composition of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> was confirmed by energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS) analysis (Figure S1, Supporting Information).
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="anie201606508-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/458c7540-40d4-4e72-9dba-f0d825607fd8/anie201606508-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/458c7540-40d4-4e72-9dba-f0d825607fd8/anie201606508-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1e24dd5b-6ef6-4851-96ce-8f919831ff32/anie201606508-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/458c7540-40d4-4e72-9dba-f0d825607fd8/anie201606508-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=anie201606508-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.201606508" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>X-ray diffraction pattern and Rietveld refinement of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>The electrochemical properties of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as a bipolar electrode material were first assessed in a three-electrode system with Ag/AgCl as the reference electrode in the aqueous electrolyte of Na<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> (1.0 <span class="smallCaps">m</span>). The cyclic voltammogram (CV) of the Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> electrode features a pair of redox peaks centered at about 0.6 V vs. Ag/AgCl (Figure <a href="#anie201606508-fig-0003">3</a> A), which can be attributed to the reversible reactions of the Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>2+</sup> redox couple in the NASICON lattice with extraction/insertion of sodium-ions from/into Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>. The redox voltage of Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>2+</sup> in the NASICON-structured Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> is well-below the oxygen evolution potential in the neutral aqueous electrolyte (1.1 V vs. Ag/AgCl), which therefore enables it to be used as a high-voltage cathode for aqueous sodium-ion batteries.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0043_R_d54212395e677" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Nano Energy">43</a>-<a href="#anie201606508-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0045_R_d54212395e677" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Electrochem. Solid-State Lett.">45</a></sup></span> In accordance with the CV results, the Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> electrode exhibited charge and discharge profiles with well-defined voltage plateaus centered at about 0.6 V vs. Ag/AgCl with little polarization (Figure <a href="#anie201606508-fig-0003">3</a> B), corresponding to the reversible reaction of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>−Na<sup>+</sup>−e<sup>−</sup>⇄Na<sub>2</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, with the oxidation of Mn<sup>2+</sup> to Mn<sup>3+</sup> on charge and the reduction of Mn<sup>3+</sup> to Mn<sup>2+</sup> on discharge,<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0046_R_d54212395e714" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - J. Mater. Chem. A">46</a>, <a href="#anie201606508-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0047_R_d54212395e714" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">47</a></sup></span> keeping the valence state of Ti<sup>4+</sup> unchanged (Figure S2, Supporting Information). The Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> electrode delivers a discharge capacity of 58.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at a rate of 0.5 C (1 C=58.7 mA g<sup>−1</sup>), corresponding to a nearly 100 % utilization of its one sodium extraction/insertion capacity of the Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> electrode through the Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>2+</sup> redox couple. The structural change of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> is reversible during extraction and insertion of one sodium-ion per formula unit through the Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>2+</sup> redox couple. When charging the electrode to 1.0 V vs. Ag/AgCl, the X-ray diffraction peaks of (012), (113), (024), and (300) shift to higher angles, indicative of a volume shrinkage because of the extraction of sodium ions from the NASICON-structured material.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0048_R_d54212395e751" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">48</a></sup></span> Upon discharging to 0 V vs. Ag/AgCl, the diffraction peaks of the electrode recovered to its original state (Figure S3, Supporting Information).
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="anie201606508-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/8068982e-c38e-43a9-bba9-7ff9032144f9/anie201606508-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/8068982e-c38e-43a9-bba9-7ff9032144f9/anie201606508-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/9681d139-0d90-49f3-ad31-7abc2408ea67/anie201606508-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/8068982e-c38e-43a9-bba9-7ff9032144f9/anie201606508-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=anie201606508-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.201606508" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>The electrochemical performance of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> for the Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>2+</sup> redox couple in a three-electrode system with Ag/AgCl as the reference electrode. A) The cyclic voltammogram of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (solid line) and the linear sweep voltammogram of the activated carbon electrode (dot line) at a scan rate of 1.0 mV<sup>−1</sup> s. B) The galvanostatic charge/discharge profiles of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> between 0 V and 1.0 V at a rate of 0.5 C.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>The redox couple of Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> in the NASICON-structured Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> was also evaluated in a three-electrode system in the aqueous electrolyte of Na<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> (1.0 <span class="smallCaps">m</span>). The main feature of the CV curves of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> is a pair of redox peaks centered at about −0.8 V vs. Ag/AgCl (Figure <a href="#anie201606508-fig-0004">4</a> A), corresponding to the reversible insertion/extraction reaction of one sodium-ion per formula unit into/from the Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> lattice operating in a reversible reaction of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>+Na<sup>+</sup>+e<sup>−</sup>⇄Na<sub>4</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>. The observed voltage of the Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> redox couple in Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> is in accordance with the voltage of the Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> redox couple in NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, which is sufficiently higher than the hydrogen evolution potential in the neutral aqueous electrolyte (−1.2 V vs. Ag/AgCl).<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0049_R_d54212395e874" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">49</a>, <a href="#anie201606508-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0050_R_d54212395e874" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Small">50</a></sup></span> The galvanostatic discharge/charge profiles revealed that the Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> electrode delivers a sodiation capacity of 58.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at a rate of 0.5 C, corresponding to almost full utilization of the Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> redox couple in Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, with the reduction of Ti<sup>4+</sup> to Ti<sup>3+</sup> upon the insertion of one sodium-ion per formula unit and the oxidation of Ti<sup>3+</sup> to Ti<sup>4+</sup> upon the extraction of the inserted sodium-ion, without changing the valence state of Mn<sup>2+</sup> (Figure S4, Supporting Information).<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0051_R_d54212395e907" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">51</a>, <a href="#anie201606508-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0052_R_d54212395e907" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Solid State Ionics">52</a></sup></span> In addition, the charge and discharge reaction of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> proceeded mostly at a flat plateau centered at about −0.8 V vs. Ag/AgCl without significant polarization, suggesting an excellent electrochemical reversibility of the Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> electrode (Figure <a href="#anie201606508-fig-0004">4</a> B). When discharging the electrode to −1.3 V vs. Ag/AgCl, the X-ray diffraction peaks of (113), (024), (211), and (300) shift to lower angles, because of a volume expansion after the insertion of sodium-ions into the NASICON-structured material.<span><sup><a href="#anie201606508-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie201606508-bib-0053_R_d54212395e924" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - J. Mater. Chem. A">53</a></sup></span> After the extraction of the inserted sodium-ions, the material transforms back completely to its original phase (Figure S5, Supporting Information).
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="anie201606508-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/7248d046-1753-4d31-9228-6d73e87a8e3f/anie201606508-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/7248d046-1753-4d31-9228-6d73e87a8e3f/anie201606508-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/0762434d-91dc-47c1-96d6-40ac4fa2b2e5/anie201606508-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/7248d046-1753-4d31-9228-6d73e87a8e3f/anie201606508-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=anie201606508-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.201606508" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>The electrochemical performance of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> for the Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> redox couple in a three-electrode system with Ag/AgCl as the reference electrode. A) The cyclic voltammogram of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (solid line) and the linear sweep voltammogram of the activated carbon electrode (dot line) at a scan rate of 1.0 mV<sup>−1</sup> s. B) The galvanostatic charge/discharge profiles of Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> between −1.3 V and 0 V at a rate of 0.5 C.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>Since the sodium-ion insertion/extraction reactions through the Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>2+</sup> and Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> redox couples in Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> take place within the electrochemical window of the aqueous electrolyte, it is thus expected a symmetric sodium-ion battery with Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as the cathode and the anode would have a high capacity utilization and a stable cycling performance in the aqueous electrolyte of Na<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> (1.0 <span class="smallCaps">m</span>). Furthermore, the combination of the Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>2+</sup> and Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> redox couples in Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> would enable the symmetric battery to possess a high output voltage of approximately 1.4 V. Figure <a href="#anie201606508-fig-0005">5</a> A illustrates the CV curve of the symmetric cell within the voltage of 0.4 V and 1.8 V in the aqueous electrolyte. The oxidation and reduction peaks were centered at about 1.4 V, which is consistent with the predicted value on the basis of the voltage difference between the Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>2+</sup> and Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> redox couples in Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>. As shown in Figure <a href="#anie201606508-fig-0005">5</a> B, the charge/discharge profiles of the symmetric cell are centered at about 1.4 V without obvious polarization, delivering a reversible capacity of 57.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at a charge/discharge rate of 0.5 C. The energy density of the symmetric cell is about 40 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> based on the total weight of the active materials in the anode and cathode, which is comparable to or higher than the conventional aqueous rechargeable batteries and the recently developed aqueous sodium-ion batteries (Table S2, Supporting Information). The rate capability of the symmetric cell is also evaluated at different charge/discharge rates from 0.5 C to 10 C (Figure <a href="#anie201606508-fig-0005">5</a> C). The reversible capacity of the symmetric cell was 56.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at the rate of 1 C, and 46.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at the rate of 10 C. When the rate was back to 0.5 C, the capacity of 57.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> was recovered, demonstrating an excellent rate capability of the symmetric cell. Importantly, about 98 % of its initial capacity can be retained for the symmetric battery after 100 charge/discharge cycles at a rate of 1 C (Figure <a href="#anie201606508-fig-0005">5</a> D), with the coulombic efficiency exceeding 99 % in the charge/discharge cycles, manifesting the high reversibility of the symmetric cell through the Mn<sup>3+</sup>/Mn<sup>2+</sup> and Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> redox couples on the cathode and anode sides, respectively, in the NASICON-structured Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="anie201606508-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/14f2a0d6-08cd-4f49-837a-6b4442646780/anie201606508-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/14f2a0d6-08cd-4f49-837a-6b4442646780/anie201606508-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/61047dfe-213c-4860-b16b-da5ef4f56deb/anie201606508-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/14f2a0d6-08cd-4f49-837a-6b4442646780/anie201606508-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=anie201606508-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.201606508" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>The electrochemical performance of the symmetric sodium-ion battery with Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as the anode and cathode in an aqueous electrolyte. A) The cyclic voltammogram of the symmetric sodium-ion battery between 0.4 V and 1.8 V at a scan rate of 1.0 mV<sup>−1</sup> s. B) The charge/discharge profiles of the symmetric sodium-ion battery between 0.4 V and 1.8 V at a rate of 0.5 C. C) The rate performance of the symmetric sodium-ion battery at different rates from 0.5 C to 10 C. D) The capacity retention and coulombic efficiency of the symmetric sodium-ion battery at a rate of 1 C.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>In conclusion, with the application of a low-cost bipolar electrode material of NASICON-structured Na<sub>3</sub>MnTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, a symmetric sodium-ion battery with an aqueous electrolyte was constructed to meet the demand of stationary energy storage. The symmetric sodium-ion battery exhibits an operating voltage of 1.4 V in the aqueous electrolyte of Na<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> with an excellent rate capability and cycle stability. The development of aqueous symmetric sodium-ion batteries with a low cost, long cycle life, high safety, high efficiency, and an environmentally-benign nature may pave the way for large-scale stationary energy storage applications and will provide new opportunities towards the advancement of room-temperature sodium-ion batteries.</p>
         
         <div class="article-section__content">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="anie201606508-sec-0002-title"> Acknowledgements</h3>

            <ol></ol>
         </div>
         </section>
